<div id="review_2020136622" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2020136622" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6217162-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430955688p2/6217162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2020136622?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/6217162-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6217162-donna?shelf=criminal-mystery">criminal-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2020136622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4768013743376331947">And Connelly hits one out of the ballpark again. How does he do it? How does he consistently produce such great stories throughout such a long writing career? It helps that he writes with as much authenticity and integrity as his characters possess. And his latest character in his newest series is no exception. <br/><br/>RenÃ©e Ballard is a young detective with 14 years of her life invested in the LA Police Department, only to see it practically go down the drain when she files sexual harassment charges ag</span>
  <span id="freeText4768013743376331947" style="display:none">And Connelly hits one out of the ballpark again. How does he do it? How does he consistently produce such great stories throughout such a long writing career? It helps that he writes with as much authenticity and integrity as his characters possess. And his latest character in his newest series is no exception. <br /><br />RenÃ©e Ballard is a young detective with 14 years of her life invested in the LA Police Department, only to see it practically go down the drain when she files sexual harassment charges against her commander. Rather than receive justice in the matter, despite there being a witness who unfortunately never came to her defense, she was punished for making waves and was assigned to working "The Late Show" which is the 11 pm to 7 am shift. Besides the crummy hours, what's worse is the lack of satisfaction during that shift when detectives may start investigations, but must turn most of them over to the day crew to follow up with and eventually solve. That's because detectives can't exactly interview people, gather clues and process them during those late and early morning hours and expect any results. But two cases RenÃ©e catches at night she refuses to let go of during the day because the victims either aren't deemed important enough to have priority or are seen as collateral damage in the larger scheme of things. Always seeking justice for the underdog as she is one herself, RenÃ©e forgoes sleep and deepens her investigations even though she has been told to stand back and stand down. And she soon discovers when continuing on that she stands to lose more than sleep as her investigations grow increasingly complicated and connect to more than she ever could have bargained for when beginning them. <br /><br />I'm a long time fan of Connelly and have read and enjoyed just about every book he has written, so it's no surprise I enjoyed this book, too. I was certainly excited to begin a new series by him, especially one featuring a female protagonist this time. Not that I haven't enjoyed reading mainly about male characters in his other series, but I was curious to see how he would develop a main female character this time when females have always played such a minor role in his other stories. So when I first started reading this book with its competent yet impulsive maverick of a detective who went off on her own against orders, I was a little disappointed because I couldn't helping thinking of her as just a female version of Harry Bosch. But soon, Connelly deftly revealed a bit more about Ballard with each new chapter and she grew into her unique self, her tragic childhood and professional background making her into a sympathetic character the reader can care about, one who is well in control of her emotions until she isn't and zings the reader right in the heart. <br /><br />As for the story, there are multiple criminal mysteries within it which have enough turns and ultimately twists to keep those pages moving through the reader's fingers. And there were plenty of heart stopping and jaw dropping moments, including the very ending with its emotional punch that made my chest ache. I only had one quibble about this book which troubled me. It was the pervasive use of female characters as victims which you may not think is unusual in a criminal mystery series. But I felt repeated instances where it occurred with sexual components was too much and it set off warning bells for me. So I hope this isn't a sign of things to come in this series. If it is, you'll hear about it from me. But aside from that, I enjoyed every bit of this book with its wonderful new main character I'd enjoy reading more about. <br /><br />What else can I say? If you've never read anything by this author, go ahead and start here as it's the first in a new series. Then start at the beginning of his other two series while waiting for more of this one. You'll have a lot of catching up to do and many pleasurable reading hours ahead of you while doing it. But if you're already a fan of Connelly, you're already all caught up in more ways than one, and you didn't need me to convince you this book would be a winner and a must read. Connelly's track record precedes him and speaks for itself, louder than any number of five star reviews.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4768013743376331947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BIC6Vg65udrJe5+0Mnyppggo+XgoTAROyHp1hgJEkIi8VKlbahyBHgyIZ6C7C3yaeWYp1G8QD3RwYoUsXiV2fA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

When Amos Decker and his FBI colleague Alex Jamison are called to London, North Dakota, they instantly sense that the thriving fracking town is ripe for trouble. The promise of a second gold rush has attracted an onslaught of newcomers all hoping for a windfall, and the community is growing faster than houses can be built. The sudden boom has also brought a slew of problems with it, including drugs, property crimes, prostitution -- and now murder.Decker and Jamison are ordered to investigate the death of a young woman named Irene Cramer, whose body was expertly autopsied and then dumped in the open -- which is only the beginning of the oddities surrounding the case. As Decker and Jamison dig into Irene\'s life, they are shocked to discover that the woman who walked the streets by night as a prostitute was a teacher for a local religious sect by day -- a sect operating on land once owned by a mysterious government facility that looms over the entire community.London is a town replete with ruthless business owners, shady government officials, and religious outsiders, all determined to keep their secrets from coming out. When other murders occur, Decker will need all of his extraordinary memory and detective skills, and the assistance of a surprising ally, to root out a killer and the forces behind Cramer\'s death. . <span id="freeTextContainer4897989912203649968"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads' database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information.</a></i> <br/><br/>Michael Connelly decided to become a writer after discovering the books of Raymond Chandler while attending the University of Florida. Once he decided on this direction he chose a major in journalism and a minor in creative writing â a curriculum in which one of his teache</span>
  <span id="freeText4897989912203649968" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads' database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a></i> <br /><br />Michael Connelly decided to become a writer after discovering the books of Raymond Chandler while attending the University of Florida. Once he decided on this direction he chose a major in journalism and a minor in creative writing â a curriculum in which one of his teachers was novelist Harry Crews.<br /> <br />After graduating in 1980, Connelly worked at newspapers in Daytona Beach and Fort Lauderdale, Florida, primarily specializing in the crime beat. In Fort Lauderdale he wrote about police and crime during the height of the murder and violence wave that rolled over South Florida during the so-called cocaine wars. In 1986, he and two other reporters spent several months interviewing survivors of a major airline crash. They wrote a magazine story on the crash and the survivors which was later short-listed for the Pulitzer Prize for feature writing. The magazine story also moved Connelly into the upper levels of journalism, landing him a job as a crime reporter for the Los Angeles Times, one of the largest papers in the country, and bringing him to the city of which his literary hero, Chandler, had written.<br /> <br />After three years on the crime beat in L.A., Connelly began writing his first novel to feature LAPD Detective Hieronymus Bosch. The novel, The Black Echo, based in part on a true crime that had occurred in Los Angeles, was published in 1992 and won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel by the Mystery Writers of America. Connelly has followed that up with over 30 more novels. <br /> <br />Over eighty million copies of Connellyâs books have sold worldwide and he has been translated into forty foreign languages. He has won the Edgar Award, Anthony Award, Macavity Award, Los Angeles Times Best Mystery/Thriller Award, Shamus Award, Dilys Award, Nero Award, Barry Award, Audie Award, Ridley Award, Maltese Falcon Award (Japan), .38 Caliber Award (France), Grand Prix Award (France), Premio Bancarella Award (Italy), and the Pepe Carvalho award (Spain) .<br /><br />Michael was the President of the Mystery Writers of America organization in 2003 and 2004. In addition to his literary work, Michael is one of the producers and writers of the TV show, âBosch,â which is streaming on Amazon Prime Video. <br /><br />Michael lives with his family in Los Angeles and Tampa, Florida.</span>
